RATING: 6
Thematic, light and silly tile-layer/racing game.

The game is divided into two parts: 1) a setup phase, where people are added to the city of Pompeii through card placement, and 2) the lava tile-laying and people movement (out of the city) phase.

In the first phase, the goal is to add as many of your people as possible to the city of Pompeii, using cards.  There is some minimal strategy in that some locations are better than others, when you add to a building with other people already there you get people growth (neighbors), and you can plan to group up with certain people.  However, there are the Omen cards, which come out randomly and these allow a player to choose any other player and dump them in the volcano (this happens ALOT in this game).  Eventually this phase ends with a particular card that comes at a semi-deterministic interval.

The second phase is where the real game starts.  Each turn, you draw a lava tile and place it adjacent to existing lava tiles of the same type (and if you happen to kill some other people, oh well!!), and then you move (race) your people towards the exits and out of the city hopefully.  Hopefully.  The game ends when all of the lava tiles have been played.  The winner is the player with the most people out of the city.

This is really a quite simple game, but it's fun, thematic, and has great components, and seems to play well from 2-4 players.  Probably a good gateway game or light filler (despite some opportunity for planning, the game can't be taken too seriously).

RATING: 5
Chaos here, chaos there, chaos everywhere. But hey, fleeeing from lava streams while heavens are pouring hot ash and rock down on you, must be a mayhem.

In boardgame terms the above means that there is luck involved with the card draw, there is luck involved with the lava tile draw, the placement of citizens and relatives is chaotic since you have no control over other players, the placement of lava tiles is chaotic, since you have no control over other players.

So the whole game is very chaotic and luck driven, but knowing this there is still some room for cunning. Good for occasional casual fun but nothing to get excited about.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Smashing!  An almost perfect light-medium game that would also be good with growing families.  The theme is fantastic.  I defy anyone who isn't oversensitive (being thrown into a volcano might not be your Aunt Maud's idea of fun) not to enjoy the idea of this - a gold star to the designer for the volcano-tossing idea alone.  Having one of your pieces, in a good position, thrown in can be excrutiating, though.  Still, you can get the rotter back and feel the exquisite pleasure of seeing his piece fry.

Play does not lack for choices and hard decisions have to be made.  Those who say the first half is without decent decisions have not grasped this one at all! (shakes head).  I've played it many times and how you place and spread your pieces, which cards in your hand you play, what order you play cards in, how you utilise neutral areas and how you move your pieces are all crucial to how you're going to do. You cannot win by not thinking.  Sometimes you have to more or less kill off some of your own pieces to get a win.  

Hey, if you've not played this, if anyone suggests it, you should jump at the chance.  You'll probably want to play it again very quickly!

Fun!  Fun!  Fun!
(and isn't that what it's all about?)

RATING: 1
The Downfall of Gaming.

An easy "1" for me. Does it work mechanically? Barely. Is it fun or humorous? Slightly (and here's where I start to have a problem with it). Should it be considered a game? No. The theme alone is distasteful and unsuitable to the notions of what a family game, a "light" game, or maybe any game should be. 

Rather than trying to help everyone escape, or fight against some sort of existential threat together, players jockey to help their own clans escape. Everyone is fundamentally a victim, and players can use the volcanic debris to kill or impede their neighbors and fellow citizens. The lowest point was throwing human sacrifices into the volcano, which bizarrely (and quite morbidly) also serves as a tie-breaker mechanic.

"Let's use the volcano to kill each other while I self-servingly help my family members to escape (and no one else). The player with the least victims wins!" All of this amounts to shameful display of human behavior that the players are asked to recreate to be successful. "Screw everyone else--run for your lives!"

The fact that the mechanics are light is also a problem, in that its lightness runs totally contrary to the immense awfulness of its theme. This would be fun and funny if it were all played for over-the-top satire, but sadly, it's not. It unknowingly satirizes itself, and perhaps many other games that abstractly depict human suffering.

Maybe the game is ahead of its time, and my standards are outdated. Maybe 2000 years from now future humans will find it fun trying to escape real disasters (natural or otherwise) from our own time, such as a tsunami, a hurricane, the Wilhelm Gustloff, a mass shooting, the Twin Towers on 9/11, or a concentration camp. Light mechanics could be applied to any human tragedy in the way this game does to produce dog-eat-dog fun for the whole family.

To me, the game represents a despicable low point in the hobby, probably more for the fact that its tastelessness was apparently unrecognized not only by its creators, but also by we board gamers. I'm not sure if it's better or worse that adults enjoy it, or that they let their children play it as well. What lessons does it teach us, exactly? 

Ultimately, we've reached a point, and this game is perhaps the epitome of that, when it's become OK to make a game for a game's sake. It shows no sensitivity to the suffering of the historical people represented, nor toward the awful decisions that it's asking its own participants to make in the name of "winning" and "fun."

RATING: 8
My wife said it best : The Carcassonne of Death! LOL.
But this is a seriously good game. In the first half you are placing members of your patrician family into locations through out the city. Every now and then this delightful card called an "omen" gets drawn that allows you to throw an opponent's family member into the volcano. Yes, there is a plastic piece that gets inserted into the board to represent Vesuvius. At a certain point in the game an "AD 79" card will be drawn that halts the first half of the game. From this point on your are attempting to get your people out of the city while drawing lava tiles to place throughout the city (a bit incorrect in the theme since Pompeii was buried in ash by pyroclastic flows but lava tile sounds better than pyroclastic flow tile I suppose) to possibly block exits from the city or to just kill other opponents' family members. A very morbid and macabre theme if you think about it too much but the game abstracts it nicely. The person who has the most family member saved when the lava tiles run out wins the game. 
For some extra added fun look up the "Doctor Who" variant on BGG. If you are a fan of the show you will love this fan-inspired variant.

RATING: 9
This is a favorite light, gateway game with a great theme.  There's some luck involved, but just the right amount for the time involved.  

It's fun trying to get your people in the houses nearest the exit, but spread out.  And when the volcano erupts the decisions on who you can save and who you can't and who you must move now and who can afford to wait are interesting but not too much of a brain-burner.  And, of course, getting the right lava tile to destroy a crowd of your opponent's people is great.

RATING: 7.5
Game play takes place over two distinct halves of the game.
First is getting people into the city of Pompeii, hopefully making use of the "Relative" rule to add even more than just one per turn.
Second is doing your best to get all your people out through the gates of the city and putting lava tiles on top of the other players pieces.
Fairly simple gameplay although possibly not the best for introducing people new to the hobby.

RATING: 6
Ok, so maybe I'm rushing my opinion of this one, with only 1 game played. But man, it was fun. Much more fun than Wrede's most famous effort (Carcassonne). I don't know why... the mechanics are really simple, and there is much more luck of the draw here than in Carcassone... but there's an undeniable charm to trying to get the most relatives possible, and an even more fun time trying to get all of your people out in time.

Plus, it's a game where, on my very first time playing it, I knew what I was doing. Very intuitive!

All that said, I wouldn't be able to play it with my wife, who hates aggressive games. It won't get much more aggressive than this... at least not for an Euro.

For now, it stands a solid 8, which might vary in the future depending on it's replayability.

UPDATE: Still a good game, but I'm burning out a little bit on it. Down to a 7.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The Downfall of Pompeii is a light and relatively short game that provides unexpected delight in tossing your rival players' pieces into an erupting volcano.  Gameplay simulates the population and evacuation of the Roman city Pompeii in the years up until the eruption of Mt. Vesuvius in A.D. 79.  Even after the signs of the volcano's impending eruption begin to show, players can continue to further populate the city and move relatives of current residents into different buildings.  There will be obvious competition for locations closest to the various gates that provide the only way to escape a gloomy volcanic fate.  Once the volcano begins erupting, players will take turns deciding where lava will flow throughout Pompeii and which two of their residents they want to move closer to / out of the city gates.  Residents sharing a location with other residents will have greater speed in moving throughout the city, while residents stuck by themselves are slower in making their way towards the gates.  Each player will relish the opportunity to send lava flowing over their opponents' resident pieces, or even using the lava to block all means of escape from the city, dooming all unlucky souls to the volcano.  Victory is determined by the number of residents each player is successfully able to escape from the city, with ties favoring the player who had the fewest number of residents tossed into the volcano.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.5
The game has a little bit of everything. It is strategical, tactical, there is a fair bit of luck involved and also has a strong push your luck element. Besides that the two distinct phases in the game give it a very unique feel. The clever card play to obtain the best positions in the first part feels very different from the 'race or die' feel of the second part. All in all this makes it a worthy addition to most gaming collections. Despite the dark theme I also feel this is a nice family game.

Gameplay: :star::star::star::halfstar::nostar:
Replayability: :star::star::star::star::nostar:
Fun/Social: :star::star::star::star::nostar:
Components: :star::star::star::halfstar::nostar:

RATING: 7
A little bit of strategy and a little more luck. Still good fun. People who can only a handle a little bit of luck probably won't like this. Very tactical.

Should be able to teach this now.

[b]Deck Seeding[/b]
Create 7 stacks of four building cards. Set aside.
Mix 25 building cards with 7 omen cards.
Draw 10 (15 w/2or3 players) and mix with AD79 card. Put on bottom.
Put remaining 22 (or 17) next.
AD79 Card next.
Add 2 stacks of 4 (from set asides) on top of that.
Give each player 1 stack of 4.
Remove left over stacks of 4 from the game.
1st player is to left of dealer/owner.

[b]Phase 1[/b]
1 piece per card play to building number

[b]-- AD79 appears --[/b]
(drawing player draw again)

[b]Phase 2[/b]
[i]Relatives[/i] - Place # of pieces equal to total number of pieces in all of building where initial piece is played.
1. in different part of same building
2. in different building of same color
3. in neutral building

[i]Wilds[/i]
If all four cards held match full buildings, then show and play a card as "wild". Wild placement is into any colored building, but NO relative placement.

[i]Omen Cards[/i]
If Omen card is drawn, player removes one piece of choice from board and throws in volcano. Draws another card until not an Omen card.

[b]--2nd AD79 appears--[/b]

[b]Phase 3[/b]
Put all cards away.
Draw lava tile ONLY for six turns. Place first on lava start square. Subsequent matches placed orthogonally.

After six turns players continue lava tile draw and placement, but then add movement. Move two different pieces per turn. Movement for each piece is equal to total number of pieces in square.

May move one single piece twice if piece is completely alone. 2nd move is then equal to total # pieces in second square.

[b]End[/b]
Game ends if all pieces escape or when last lava tile is played. All remaining pieces are thrown into the volcano. Count pieces for score. Winner is player with most escaped pieces. Ties won by player with [i]least[/i] pieces in volcano.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
What a great gateway style game.  The way that you can teach this game in stages makes it very accessible to all players.  I can see that there's a lot of strategy to a more experienced player, but it's lots of fun for your first time as well.  There's almost a balancing mechanism because if one player is extremely successful at getting people on the board, others will rush to kill that player's people.

The setup of the deck is a bit time-consuming.  Also you have to be comfortable with a game where you openly attack the other players.  Still there's so much nastiness going around that it's hard to get too upset.  I've had a ton of fun with this game and expect it will become one of our favorites for years to come.

RATING: 6
A very light filler game, that has a strong theme. The game is divided in two distinct phases. The rise and fall of Pompeii. In the first phase you try to get as many meeples on the board, and close to the city's exits. Incidently someone gets hit by a flying boulder from the volcano that's about to erupt. The second phase is about getting as many meeples outside the city borders when the magma starts to flow through the premises. All meeples who suffer a burning death get thrown into the volcano. Winner is the player who got the most people out. Ties are won by the player who has the least amount of meeples in the volcano.

Not much strategy in this one. Getting many meeples on the board can be a boon or a bane. Instinct would say that more meeples in the city means a higher chance more could escape the wrath of the volcano. However, more meeples also means more can die, and you don't get more turns to let them flee than your opponent. With more meeples dead, you lose the tie, which is important because scores often are pretty close.

I like it enough to play it once in a while. It's so simple anyone can join in, and although the meeples look abstract, you're constantly busy tring to save them. It's lively enough to be fun.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
2-4 | (4) | 45 min | 10+ | Klaus-Jürgen Wrede
Light, short, silly (in a good way) eurogame. There are two phases: first, players place their pawns via cards, then the volcano erupts and players move their pawns to flee the city while drawing and placing lava tiles with which they can kill others' pawns or block city exits. Gameplay is far from deep (in fact, the Omen cards can be annoyingly random), but the whole experience is a lot of fun, no matter who wins. Throwing dead pawns into the volcano is a guilty pleasure. Truly enjoyable.

RATING: 9
This game is a blast to play with the family.  One of the few games in which you actually enjoy being killed because you get to scream as someone throws you into the fiery pit of a volcano.  I like the fact that it has two distinct phases; it never gets old or boring, even for my 7-year-old, because the mechanics of the game shift completely half-way through.  My son creamed the rest of us in the first game.  The adults were all trying to slowly move people out from the interior of the city, and he moved out the ones closest to the exits.  We also managed to play this in less than an hour the first time, even with someone who has analysis paralysis.  Perfect family game.  If your family has Ticket to Ride, Settlers, and Blokus, get this next.

RATING: 5
I love to see folks complain about the "luck element" in a game about throwing people into a volcano.  This is a fairly fun game somewhat similar to Survive (although not as good) that plays in two distinct phases- a setup/placement phase that is somewhat boring, and then a more exciting, nasty, run-for-your-life phase.  It's one of the better Euros I've played in a while because it's A) actually fun B) has actual competition in it and C) there's plenty of death and destruction to mete out to the other players.  It's also a pretty short game, in the 45-60 minute range.  I don't know if it's something I'd play a lot (or more than twice), but every now and then this would be pretty entertaining as long as no one brought a copy of Survive.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A classic! It's such an unusual game, in that it consists of several parts, all of which have different gameplay and tactics. 
There is a LOT of luck, but it's just so much fun.
And this completely disproves the old 'euro-games have no theme' argument: this is dripping with theme! This game tells the story of Pompeii from arriving in the city, omens of disaster, inviting relatives to join you, making sacrifices to the gods, and finally fleeing the city as the volcano erupts. 
And you get to throw your opponents in a volcano!!!



=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
The 2nd Euro game I played and the first with my friends. I wanted to buy another gateway game, after buying Ticket to Ride and playing with family, but this time I wanted a game to play with my friends, which I think would like confrontational games, so I wanted a game with a better theme. I played it with 3 people and they loved it. I think the paper model volcano and Pompeii theme makes it really easy to get into the spirit of the game and I was amazed by the "clean" feel of the gameplay. Hardly any fiddly bits (as compared to Last Night on Earth) and really fast game play. This is the game that made me want to buy more Euro games, as I found Ticket To Ride too light, although my cousins loved it. I was surprised that we could sort of roleplay the game a bit which added to the fun.

RATING: 9
Tried this one based on recommendations read here on bgg when I was a newbie and its been a hit with the family!  Who doesn't love throwing people into a volcano?  Excellent gateway game that really grabs the attention of new gamers with 2 phases of gameplay comprised of an amalgam of mechanics (hand management,worker placement,area control and then tile-laying with a race component) that work so well together as a surprisingly simple introduction to eurogames.  The only downside I see on this one is the fiddly deck set up - not a big deal once you get used to it, but I think might turn off new gamers unless they have someone to lead them through it the first time (one of the only reasons I hesitate to give this as a gift unless I'm pretty sure I can be there to teach the first game).  Also has a significant "take that!" component which some kids (or adults) may not like.  Overall, a great family game!

RATING: 5
There's stuff to like in here to be sure. Running away from the hot lava death is fun, of course. My bar for owning a game is pretty high these days, though, and this one didn't meet the bar due to two things, both related to the Omen cards: 1) There's no downside to getting omen cards--it's pure goodness, and yet it's completely random when and how many each player get. And 2) The Omen cards have the "pick on another player at random" mechanism, which is among my current top least enjoyable mechanisms.
I bought it when I thought that would be the only way to play it, but when I played someone else's before opening mine, I sold it.

RATING: 6
Brought home as a souvenir from a trip to Grenoble, France. The game is lightweight, but very fun, and never fails to evoke hoots of laughter or appreciative comments. Why this game was never picked up by any major Dutch label will be forever beyond me: it has delightful mechanics, a rock-solid subject, plenty of good-natured take-that gameplay which turns the most peace-loving person into a rabid sadist once the lava, erm, 'gets' another victim, and is easy to learn as a final bonus. It reminds me of Emerald in many ways, but the subject is better tied to the mechanisms, although I'm still not sure why people get to have more movement points as meeples are clustered together. It's also somewhat odd that you can get to safety near a city gate on the foot of the volcano... But other than that, good, clean fun in a simple package. Go get it while it's 'hot'!

[b]Update[/b] I still think this is a charming game, but with more emphasis on 'charming' than on 'game'. Game-wise it is actually rather weak, because there isn't much you can do to change your fate, and people generally have a good idea how to make moves which cause maximum damage. There's also a nagging suspicion that the game is self-balancing in that the more people you get into Pompeji, the harder it becomes to get them out because you need to make more moves. Game-technically the game lost two points because of this, but I'm giving it back one point because of the 'whole package' so to speak, a rare occasion.

RATING: 7
The subject matter may be a little dark, but this game is lighthearted.  It's a good mix of strategy and fun.  The two phases of the game could be disjointed, but the designer cleverly set up the mechanics such that you need to think about the second phase as you place markers in the first phase.  Very enjoyable with 2, but I found it to be a bit too random with 4 players.

My main complaint with this game is that the ending/winner can become a foregone conclusion before you're truly finished - it's akin to throwing in your hand before playing the last trick in Euchre.  It's not a huge deal, but I just don't enjoy that aspect.

RATING: 6
Components: Beautiful board, with lots of ambient details that add to the theme without detracting from the functionality. The cards are simple, but easy on the eyes. The tiles are up to Amigo standards, though there could perhaps have been a more gushing-lava design to them, rather than the veins of lava they now sport.

Experience: Very interesting two-phase game. Both phases feature limited numbers of attractive moves, yet there are engaging decisions to be made. The first phase is very different from the second; in the first, players budget their cards to cleverly get as many followers on the board as possible, and nearest the exits; in the second phase, it is a puzzle, a la Chinese Checkers, to efficiently transport followers toward the exits. There is a lot of chaos in the final attack of the lava, but the game moves quickly enough that the final phase seems exciting rather than anti-strategic.

First Played: 2005-01-24
Last Played: 2010-01-11
Eagerness to Play Again: Within a year

Plays (2):
2 players: 1
3 players: 1

RATING: 5

The most difficult thing to explain is that there are two separate phases--moving people in, and then having them run away from the lava.  Once this is understood, the game flows (har har) well.

RATING: N/A
$20 BGG
The game falls into two halves: before and after the eruption of Vesuvius. Before the eruption, players play cards to place their pieces in buildings. After the first eruption, they can also place as many relatives as the number of pieces already in the building they placed their piece in. When Omen cards are drawn, the player can take any opponent's piece and throw it into the erupting volcano. In this manner, players try to get as many pieces onto the board as close to the exits from the city as possible.

RATING: 5
I will probably have to play this again, but IMO is one of the few games that is *obviously* overrated here on BGG.

Rating after 1 play, will play it again before trading it anyway ^_^

I mean, come on, the first phase is borderline random and, probably, really much more complicated/long than it should. If Klaus had streamlined the game to create a more linear and quicker first phase, this would've probably been a nice family game, since the second phase, although very obvious, decisions wise, is at least fun. As it stands, the decision you have to make in the first half really don't matter that much.  Maybe there should be some variant added to lessen the luck of the draw in the first phase (e.g. You can play 2 cards as a single wild card, but from that point on, your hand is reduced to only 3 cards and so on)

RATING: 8
An enjoyable co-petitive game themed around the destruction of Pompeii.  More could probably have been done with it, but as it stands it is a thoroughly entertaining game.  The strategy of placing one's people on the historically-derived map is broken into two highly competitive stages of escalating importance.  Appeasing omens of doom adds a competitive dimension to this process and indulges everyone's dark side as they feed rivals to the volcano.  Once the eruption starts, a tense dance begins in which players attempt to evacuate their people from the city while simultaneously looking for opportunities to hinder their opponents.  The process is made more tricky by the need not to hinder one's own escape.

RATING: 7.5
Interesting little filler game that has two distinct halves. The fill-up-town phase and the run-for-your-lives phase. 

The intital phase is card reliant and you suffer if you do not draw similar cards to your opponents however if you do too well here players notice you have more pieces than them and thus into the volcano you go whenever there is an omen drawn. 

There is a really interesting mechanic for flocking together, but and the same time you wish for all your pieces to be spread throughout the city. There is some nice strategy there, such as if my piece is stood with yours you are not going to put lava over your own piece so mine is 'safe' too but if all players bar one flock to the same location that space looks mighty tempting to the player that doesn't have a piece stood there.

The second phase is entirely different to the first worker placement phase. This phase has tile laying and movement point allowances as you rush to have all your meeple flee before they burn to a crisp.

Tile placement is straightforward you must place the lave flow adjacent to the symbol that appears on the tile, the new dual sides tiles are a really nice addition as you are able to choose a little more where you wish the lava to flow. Tile placement also happens before you are allowed to move so you can't flee and then burn everyone you left behind.

You then have two movement actions where each movement allowance is the number of meeple initially in the square. This is a very interesting mechanic as you wish to piggyback off other players pieces but don't want to wait so long you get left behind and have to plod towards the exit gateways as lava creeps closer.

I really enjoyed the game and there is novelty in throwing opponents meeple into the volcano however the number of meeple in the volcano as a tie breaks doesn't really seem to work as several of us has the same number of crispy meeple. I wish the initial placement phase was longer and I may try a variant whereby players have a hand of three cards instead of four thus the deck is larger to see how this affects gameplay.

Components are really good except for the cloth bag which feels very cheap. The volcano is sturdy plastic and fits together very well and the artwork used is really nice and the theme fits very well. Overall really happy with this game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A hit for me, although it has a negative element. You lay numbered/coloured cards to put your people in the city. Then the volcano erupts and you place lava tiles, and start moving your people out through the gates. Any that get burnt or trapped are dropped into the crater (and become the tie-break). The most escapees wins, the least in the crater is the tie-break.

Quick, simple decisions and fun, but you are attacking the other players and actively killing people, which is macabre.

RATING: 4
Move with your family and relatives to the flourishing city of Pompeii, before racing them to safety when the Vesuvius erupts!

There are choices, but they're rather meaningless.
Relatives are an interesting mechanic, but the omen cards are too random and have a huge impact on the result of the game.
In 2-player games lava flows too slowly and I think there should be a few more lava tokens; the endgame seems to play itself and the outcome has already been decided previously, so the lava phase feels even more of a drag. Let me choose 2 of the 6 lava groups, and let me place one new lava tile for each! If I can't place 2, drop that groups thing and make all the lava the same!

This game can be fun only if you're having a laugh with your friends while you burn their family and relatives.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
In the first phase meeples are moved into Pompeii, in the second phase those same people are then evacuated again while Vesuvius unloads its lava on the city. Everyone tries to get their own people to safety while at the same time gobbling everyone else with the lava streams.

Both the placement and evacuation phases are controlled by randomly drawn cards or tiles, respectively. The decisions to make are usually pretty obvious (move into buildings close to the city gates, preferably those which are already inhabited to get a maximum number of meeples deployed; move away from lava towards the exits) and not particularly taxing. Neither do they have an especially strong impact on the game as a whole. Pompeii is a fine family game, although some may find it a bit confrontational for that, and I'm sure those who simply like to throw their opponents into a volcano will have a hoot, too. There is not a lot of substance beneath the layers of ash and fire, however.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Downfall of Pompeii is a thematically excellent game (even if it's not really that accurate to the history).  It's pretty random at the beginning. The placement phase was obviously designed to just get the pieces out in a random, but somewhat evenly spread manner. But the Omen cards keep things spicy and the Relatives rule allows for some tactical placement options.  The real game is in the second phase where the lava comes out to destroy Pompeii! This is where the fun is - slightly gimmicky with the 3D volcano, but it is part of the charm. You do have to put some thought into tile placement and movement, so that works just enough to keep you into it until the game ends. Overall, DoP has quite a few aching moments and even a spot of tension, but is a little too simple and random to have any serious depth. Still, it wins on enough notes to be a happy inclusion to my gaming library!

RATING: 7.3
We like to have more citizens on the board when Vesuvius erupts! So we use a house rule for where to insert the AD79 card (the 2nd time).
Instead of shuffling it into the bottom 15 cards of the deck; we place it:
in the bottom 12 cards for 2 player games
in the bottom  9 cards for 3 player games
in the bottom  8 cards for 4 player games

We also limit the Omen cards for 2 player games. If you draw an Omen card, instead of discarding it, play it face up in front of the player you're using it on. You can't play an Omen card on a player that has 2 more face up Omens in front of him than you do.


If a player runs out of pieces he has the option to call for an early eruption, as one does when one's cards are all for full buildings.

RATING: 8
Downfall of Pompeii is a game of two halves, fueled by hand management and some tile placement. At first, players play cards to place pieces on the board in certain houses. Then, partway through the game, lava will begin to flow and now it is time to escape the city with the pieces earlier placed. Pompeii is a perfect level of depth for what it tries to achieve. Games are light and breezy, but offer just enough strategic depth where choices are meaningful yet low steaks. The components are great, in a quirky board game way. It is fun tossing tokens into the volcano as the lava flows expand. Pompeii is immediately appealing and approachable.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
The Downfall of Pompeii is one of those rare games wherein my opinion has improved dramatically over time.  The first time I played, I was expecting a deeper game, filled with drama and strategic options.  I was disappointed, and found the lengthy placement portion of the game to be quite dull.  The race for the exits was better, and more fun, but it didn’t salvage the game.  Fortunately, I did give the game another chance, and found that I enjoyed the experience considerably more.  I believe it was a matter of accepting the game for what it is:  a light, fun romp.  While there are some decisions to be made, the game isn’t a deep strategic affair.  Rather, it is seems meant to be little more than a fun pastime.  In that light, it succeeds brilliantly.

While still not terribly titillating, the placement phase does have its purpose.  Decisions must be made where to place citizens.  Do you place them in buildings near the gates, so they can make quick exits when the volcano erupts?  Do you try to take advantage of the "relative" rule to place numerous citizens with as many placements as possible, knowing that this will likely cause you to bear the brunt of the omen cards?  Do you place into the somewhat safer central part of the city, hoping to make fast sprints to the exits and outrun the lava flows?  These are important decisions, but none of them seem to be that critical, as there are pros and cons to each approach, and ultimately they all seem to be of fairly equal value.

Choosing which citizens to move on a turn seems even less important, as the lava appears in a very random fashion.  A safe spot can suddenly become dangerous and untenable, while a building located adjacent to a lava flow may go turn-after-turn without being engulfed.  Generally, the idea is to save who you can, and abandon the rest.  Cruel, but effective.

I’m happy to see Mayfair bringing this game to a wider audience.  It is virtually identical to the original Amigo version, with the only real change being an improved, plastic volcano to replace the fragile paper original.  I’m not sure just how much appeal the game will have with the general public, as the deadly theme is certainly to cause some consternation and objections in some circles.  For those willing to look past such things, however, The Downfall of Pompeii offers a fun gaming experience and stands in stark contrast to the grim tragedy of the actual event.

RATING: 7
Menekülj, amíg nem késő…
Már az elején tisztázzuk le. Ez egy olyan játék, amiben a résztvevők egymással tolnak ki. Ez a játék része, nem kerülhető el. Így az érzelmesebb lelkületű játékosok keressenek mást maguknak.
Még a játék kipróbálása előtt felkeltette érdeklődésemet a játék alapszituációja: Pompeji városának pusztulása. Szerintem ezt mindenki ismeri. A játék ezt az alapot kiaknázva 2 részben teszi próbára a játékosokat. A legbonyolultabb dolog a húzópakli elkészítése lesz, mert a szabályok egyszerűek. Alapból 4 kártyával indulsz, majd egyet-egyet kijátszva körödben próbálod a nálad lévő lakosokat a legjobb helyekre letenni. Ám egyszer a vulkánunk füstölögni kezd és új szelek fújnak a városban. Most már minden jó helyre letett lakosodért plusz rokonokat hozhatsz be és néha egy-egy lakost szépen feláldoznak az Isteneknek. Sajnos ez sem segít és a vulkán ki fog törni. A láva elszabadul a városban, majd a játékosok először a gonosz vulkán képében tovább terjesztik a bezúduló lávát, majd megpróbálják a legtöbb lakosukat kimenekíteni a városból. Előre szólók, hogy mindet nem tudod megmenteni. Ha ezzel a ténnyel meg tudsz birkózni, remek élményben lehet részed. Bár a vulkánból folyó láva megjelenése és terjedése szerencsefüggő (igaz a játék vége felé ki lehet számolni, hogy mi van még a húzózsákban), azonban a játék elején mindenképpen taktikázni kell és azért dolgozni, hogy a második részben minél több rokont hozz a játékba. Hogy az a célszerűbb, ha egy helyre összpontosítod lakosaidat vagy szétszóród őket a városban, már legyen az a feladvány, amelyet játék közben tudsz megfejteni. :)

RATING: N/A
It's a fun game that plays in an hour, and I love the 2 distinct flavored "phases" to the game. The first half is tactical card play to try to get a sufficient # of meeples on the board. Then... all of a sudden... Mt. Vesuvius strikes and the cards are immediately put away and it becomes a tile-laying game of survival. Stay clear of the red tiles! Run for your lives!!! There's (temporarily) safety in numbers.

For some reason the game came pre-designed with a dwindling # of colored pawns. So for a 2 player game, you use 2 exact colors. For a 3 player game, you use the same 2 colors + a 3rd, etc. Just thought I would mention that in case you notice there isn't the same # of tokens per color. I think it was a silly excuse to save a $ buck or two on the production.

RATING: 6
Only one play, need to get a couple more in to really get a feel for it. That said, here are my initial impressions.

The comparisons to Survive are not without merit. Certainly thematically I can see why this is the case. Unfortunately, compared to Survive, there seem to be far fewer important decisions. Survive is often a matter of predicting what others will do, deciding how risky to be with the rolls of the creatures, and even bluffing about values. On the other hand, Pompeii seems to simply have optimal or sub-optimal choices. Place extra people if you can. Kill other people with lava if you can. If you can get someone out, you should. If you can't, you should get them as close as possible. These very simple and obvious rubrics seem to govern the entire game. Ultimately, this just seems a bit too shallow for my tastes. But again, the first glance is not always correct so I want to give this one another couple plays to be sure.

RATING: 8
[Initial Impression: 8]
This morbidly-themed game erupts into surprising bouts of fun.  The game is played in two stages: first players place their residents into buildings governed by card play, then the volcano erupts and players attempt to move their residents out of the city to safety while placing lava tiles to impede their opponents. During the first phase, there is a lot of luck of the draw, with some spots on the board being closer to exits and therefore more desirable.  There's also a mechanism of "relatives" where you get to place more residents if the building you enter already contains residents.  If you don't draw the cards for buildings where others have been placing residents, you'll get to place fewer total residents than other players.  However, the player with the most residents on the board is not necessarily at an advantage, because they may not have enough turns to get all of their residents out of the city.  Plus, having more residents means that you'll likely get targeted by the lava tiles from other players and that you'll have more residents in the volcano at the end, which means that you'll lose in the event of a tie.  The strategy is all about trying to set yourself up in the first phase, given the cards you hold, to quickly escape in the second phase.  But the second phase, after the volcano erupts, is where all the fun resides.  Who can resist tossing their friends into the volcano to burn? And what's better than the satisfaction of barely escaping from the lava flows? The game plays fast enough that you can go several bouts in the same session, and the fun factor is hard to over-estimate.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6.75
Another www.yucata.de game.

Clever game.  The mechanics work well.  If the unique, but somewhat morbid, theme doesn't bother you, the game can be fun.

Since perfect information regarding scoring and potential scoring is available once endgame approaches, the leader (or perceived leader) is going to be picked on by the other players.  Of course, if the other players don't pull the 'right' lava tiles to incinerate or cut off the leader's people . . . 

Based on a limited sample size, the game is much better with 3 or 4 players.  Not yet sold on this one as a two player game (an unequal draw of Omen cards can really tilt the game).  If I had to guess, I'd say the 'sweet spot' for the game is 3 players.

Overall, not a great game, but a reasonably good one.  Not convinced that there are a lot of different strategies to employ though, so not sure about how much replayability there is.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The Euro version of 'Survive'  

A light fun very well themed game easy to teach and learn with a little take that runs 30 to 45 minutes which is similar to Survive in all those ways. I think there could be just a very small touch more strategy here but the difference is a pittance really, the bigger difference could be a slight bit more chaos in Survive but that is arguable also as slight temporary alliances can be formed in Survive. So then the biggest difference for me is Survive does seem just slightly more fun and this is partly due to the chaos and action that starts right away in the game where as the first half or so of Pompeii you are trying to place your guys as close to the exits as possible.  

They both have roughly the same amount of luck which is substantial but not a problem at this game length or weight. I prefer the aspect of Survive which utilizes hidden values of the people and the intrigue, guessing and bluffing that it introduces which adds a little more fun IMO, Pompeii is missing this aspect but it could be added I think (sharpie) which would up the fun a little more and also add a another slight strategic element. 

Now don't get me wrong I think this game definitely stands on its own just fine, however undeniably both games are quite similiar and scratch the same itch. Both are also good at what they were designed to do so for me owning just one suffices and I would be happy with either but glad I have Survive for the hidden value aspect. 

Overall a very well themed gateway game for 2 - 4 or occasional fun filler for weeknights. It plays like a meaty filler and when regarded as such its quite good for what it is in that sense.

RATING: 4
2016-03-14

Initial Rating: 5.0 (January 2011)

My last The Downfall of Pompeii game was a long time ago. It is a game similar to Survive, but I like Survive better. I never liked much the game and I’m not sure why. It seems to me that the game doesn’t have much in the strategy department. Most moves are kind of obvious and it has lots of “take that” and “attack the current leader”, which I don’t enjoy now. It also has a lot of uncontrollable luck (but at least it plays very quick).

Perhaps I would have liked the game better as a kid, but these days I see no point in playing it.

Bottom line, The Downfall of Pompeii can a be a good family game, however it is way too light for my current tastes. The decisions are rather obvious and luck plays a large factor in the victory.

Current Rating: 4.0

RATING: 7
I had a ton of fun with this. It brought back the fun of Survive! (a.k.a Escape From Atlantis). 

I just really enjoyed it. It's full of interactions, laughter (with good spirited players), tactical reactions (once the lava starts flowing), and some decent setup up strategy in planning for the mayhem.

The tossing of the other player's guys into the volcano allows for very tight games once you've seen it in action...besides, it's just fun to make sizzling noises.

A light game, not one to play a million times in a row, but great to bring out. One that I just enjoyed for playing and it works with a wide range of players and families.

There is a chance that bad sports could go nuts when their little wooden bits go into a paper volcano because of a cardboard square drawn at random, (though, admittedly placed with intent); and if that happens, the poor sport will have clearly shown that they have forgotten that it's a game, but I've not run into that and would be stunned if I did.

RATING: 10
This is a wonderful family-friendly (... and maybe not so friendly) game of hand management and area control that plays out in two distinct phases.  Place as many of your people as close to the 7 exit gates as possible to ensure their chances of getting out in time before Mount Vesuvius suddenly and unexpectedly decides to exercise her mighty wrath (insert sound effects here).  There's a great deal of satisfaction in placing a lava tile in front of an exit gate just before your opponent has a chance to escape to safer ground (again, more sound effects)

Mwha,ha,ha,ha,haaaaa... I LOVE this game!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
An excellent, excellent game.  

While it's not "heavy" on strategy, there's plenty of strategy available here.  Don't listen to those discounting this game as a luck-fest (though, admittedly, more luck is introduced with more players).    

The game takes place over two distinctly different (yet related) phases.  These two phases feel quite different mechanically and, yet, remain cohesive and thematic.  This is great accomplishment in streamlined game design that offers a lot of replayability.  I would welcome an edition with better/updated artwork, but the components are quite sufficient as is (note: I have the older edition, which I hear is superior in its component quality).  

This is an anchor in my collection.

RATING: 8
Based on one play with four people.  Very dramatic for a light game -- love the tension of trying to escape the lava flow and the way the city becomes increasingly desolate.

My one qualm is the subtle quirks in the rules, as the game moves through what are really four distinct phases.  At different phases you have to change your focus from whether a building is the same color, to whether it is separate from another building of the same color, and then to city squares instead of buildings.  I'm eager to try this with my family, but a little apprehensive about whether they will tolerate the subtleties of the rules.  It definitely is more fiddly than say Ticket to Ride.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
The game falls into two halves: before and after the eruption of Vesuvius. Before the eruption, players play cards to place their pieces in buildings. After the first eruption, they can also place as many relatives as the number of pieces already in the building they placed their piece in. When Omen cards are drawn, the player can take any opponent's piece and throw it into the erupting volcano. In this manner, players try to get as many pieces onto the board as close to the exits from the city as possible.

After the second eruption, the game changes. Now each player places a lava tile, which kills any pieces on that square and may block exits from the city. Then they move two pieces toward the exits, moving them a number of squares equal to the pieces on the square from which they started. The player who gets the most pieces out of the city wins.

RATING: 5
Fun thematic game and the challenge builds up as things get "hot" in Pompeii and players try to position themselves within the city in order to exit the volcanic lava and ashe.  

However, after a subsequent playing, I find that it's a little underwhelming in that not all locations or squares are balanced.  I don't believe that all squares have a "relatively equivalent" threat of lava moving on to that square.  There are too few lava tiles per symbol and the whole city does not get engulfed in lava.  (This is suppose to be the Titanic and this luxury liner/ship must sink, in the end.)  I believe that if each of the six lava symbols have at least 2 to 4 more tiles in the draw bag, that will create sufficient lava threat to all squares in the city.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A bit in the mold of Survive! you seek to get as many of your pawns to safety outside the city as possible.  Three phases exist within the game:  1) initial placement of individual pawns based on card draw, 2) placement of more pawns based on card draw and an opportunity to place additional relatives (more pawns) based on number of pawns already in building, 3) the volcanoe erupts and you just lay a lava tile (hopefully burying your opponents in the lava flow) and move 2 of your pawns a certain number of spaces (based on number of pawns in starting square).  Fun game as long as everyone is fully aware this is an elimination game and not a friendly game...
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Ez egy kis helyigényű, nagyon könnyen tanulható, hangulatos, könnyed, gonoszkodós játék. Kifejezetten ajánlható a társasjátékokkal épp csak ismerkedőknek is.

Két részből áll a játék. Az első részben Pompei városának benépesítésével telik, a játékosok véletlenszerűen húzott kártyalapok segítségével próbálnak minél több embert a városba telepíteni. Itt elég kevés a lehetőség a stratégiázásra, szerencsefüggő, hogy ki milyen lapokat húz, ezáltal mely épületekbe rakhatja az embereit, de olyan nagyon nagy jelentősége talán nincs is. A fázis végére nagyjából ugyanannyi embere lesz mindenkinek Pompeiben. Persze, gonoszkodni már itt is lehet: az Omen kártya felhúzásakor egy tetszőleges embert a városból a vulkánba lehet dobni, onnantól az a bábu kikerül a játékból. A vulkán a város mellett van, egy papírból készült csúcs nélküli kúpot kell elképzelni, amibe igen jó érzés az ellenfél emberkéit bedobálni. Hangulatból ötös.

Amikor már nagyjából telepakolták a játékosok a várost az embereikkel, egyszer csak kitör a vulkán. Innentől aztán végképp gonoszkodóssá válik a játék: a játékosok felváltva irányítják a várost elpusztító lávát, hogy merre folyjon, és minden a láva útjába kerülő bábu rögtön a vulkánba kerül. A láva irányításán felül még két lépésnyit mozgatják is a játékosok a bábujaikat, akiknek célja, hogy elérjék a város valamelyik kapuját és megmeneküljenek a vulkán elől. Tehát mindenki rohan a kijáratok felé, mögöttük hömpölyög a láva, az emberek pedig sorra válnak a vulkán áldozatává, néhányan meg megmenekülnek. Az győz, akinek a legtöbb embere kijut élve a városból.

Van még pár szabály, amiktől még élvezetesebbé válik a játék. Az egyik, hogy a benépesítés fázisban ha olyan épületbe rakjuk a bábunkat, ahol már vannak egyéb emberek is, annyi extra embert felrakhatunk, amennyien voltak abban az épületben (persze nem rekurzívan). A másik, hogy meneküléskor annyi mezőnyit tud lépni egy-egy ember, ahányan a kiinduló mezőjén álltak.

A játékidő elég rövid, gyorsan megy a játék, nagyon keveset kell a többiekre várni, senki nem unatkozik.

Mint írtam ez egy nagyon hangulatos, szórakoztató játék, amit nem szabad, de nem is lehet túl komolyan venni. Gonoszkodni lehet és muszáj is benne, ezért nagyon sértődősöknek nem ajánlott. Mindenki másnak viszont igen. Ez a játék az interakcióról szól, folyamatosan hatnak egymásra a játékosok, itt senki nem magának játszogat, állandó a kölcsönhatás. Stratégia nem sok van benne, ez inkább egy taktikai játék, amikor mindig az adott helyzetből próbáljuk a legtöbbet kihozni. Elsőre is tökéletes játékélményt nyújt, és egy kezdő is legyőzheti azt, aki más rengetegszer játszott vele. Ez egy tényleg szórakoztató, könnyed játék, amit szívesen vesz elő az ember. Ajánlom.

RATING: 9
This game flew under my radar and I completely forgot how I heard about it.  Anyway, I made a blind buy and have not been disappointed.  There is some incorrect math in the rules about what cards get combined with what deck and how many cards you should have left over.  Don't let that discourage you.  I got really hung up on that and hadn't started playing until I figured out either the rules were incorrect or I was shorted cards in the deck.  Regardless, the game takes place in a few stages.  One, you place your Pompeii citizen markers in the town in various buildings.  Two, the volcano eventually blows its top and you start laying lava tiles while trying to evacuate your people.  Players take turns laying tiles so you can box someone in or just flat out drop a tile on them and wipe out everyone in a building.  Brilliant game!

RATING: 5
[GAMEID=13004] feels like two games in one, although the first part just feels like a prolonged setup for the main game.  There is a little cardplay with moving your pieces into the city.  The volcano is then triggered and then there is a mad rush to get out of the city, with the ominous pieces of lava chasing after them.  Doomed meeples for some reason get ejected through the air into the volcano.  Unfortunately, dropping meeples into the volcano was not as fun as advertised.  It's a fairly light, more social game rather than a deeply analytical one (it felt much lighter than even [GAMEID=822] for example).

However, the game didn't sit well with us with just two players.  The cardplay in the first part of the game lacked any tension, as we were able to place our pieces without very much restriction.  The second part also didn't feel very tense.  Part of the reason is that you have so many pieces in the city and your turn comes up more often between placing lava tiles---with more players, there's more time for the lava to be a threat before you can move your meeples again.  

Although it seems like it should be a fun game, it just didn't work for us with two players.  Probably much better with more.

RATING: 8
We really like this one. The first phase of the game seemed a bit mechanical at first but, once we played it a few times, it got more interesting. Some of the spots on the board are clearly more desirable than others, and there is a fair amount of fun involved in trying to stake out those locations. Also, the more people you can get on the board, the better the chances of getting them off the board. This makes for great competition, using the relative rule, to place people in nearly complete buildings.

Once the volcano erupts, the game gets really fun. You can almost feel the terror of trying to flee the molten lava. :-) Seriously, the challenge of balancing the desire to get people out of the city with the challenge of keeping others away from the lava is fun. Stomping your opponents with lava tiles is a blast. And, of course, there are all the requisite screaming sounds that need to be emulated as the people are consumed by lava and tossed into the volcano.

Overall, a light but fun game. Eventually, I am sure we will tire of the game, but for now it is high on our list.

RATING: 5
An enjoyable light eurostyle game with a great theme.  The lava phase is by far the more fun of the phases.  Make sure you shuffle the Omen cards well.  If they are all in a row - one person will benefit too much.  The beginning seeding of the cards is a pain and non-intiutive. The game felt too balancing to me as the more people you get to place in the first round, the more likeliehood that you will lose them to the lava.  Using wooden cylinders for people kind of takes away from the theme.  Maybe slightly larger tokens with pictures of running people would have been better.  Overall, this one misses the mark because it is too balanced and offers too little control for a gamer's game, but the placement phase of the game is too complicated (relatives) for a family game.

RATING: 9
Wow is this one a gem. The game plays in two phases, that each feel like a game in itself. Has a lot of interesting mechanics that are exciting. Playing a card gives you a meeple on the board, but waiting until other meeples are in that area allow you to place even more meeples, kind of like a combo. Then during the next phase you are laying lava tiles out onto the board and burning enemy's meeples and throwing them into the volcano!! In a take-that manner. Meanwhile trying to escape your dudes out of the city while the lava is flowing. Movement of meeples out of the city is equal to the amount of meeples on that square, giving it a bit of a mancala feel. You find yourself rooting for the lava, and taking an odd amount of pleasure in throwing other people into the volcano. This game is freaking awesome. It mixes mechanics with a refreshingly original theme. From the maker of Carcassonne, this game reminds most people of Survive: Escape from atlantis, however Pompeii is much better if you ask me.

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Game in a Nutshell: Move you and your extended family into Pompeii only to have the nearby volcano erupt soon after sending everyone fleeing for their lives. He who saves the greater number of their own family members wins!

Played as: 4 player (2 player on Yucata.de)

Pros: Ah, the fun of running from an exploding volcano. One of the best progression of phases to match a theme in any game I've played. The game isn't overly complex and an easy one to jump right into and teach while playing. Who doesn't want to throw your gaming partners / family members in a volcano from time to time? Well this game gives you that and it actually feels satisfying. Comes with a pretty sweet plastic volcano.

Cons: Has a few clunky rules (building the starting deck and relatives) and the first half of the game is nothing to get overly excited about. The game won't satisfy gamers looking for a heavy amount of control and strategy. A little too random to allow for a pure spiteful free-for-all, and spitefulness is where the game shines. 

Other: I imagine this game being an excellent family game. The rules aren't too much for the kiddies and they ought to love throwing Mom and Dad in the volcano. I guess I better start having kids so I can find out if I'm right. Until then, I guess I'll have fun watching cities and people burn with other adults. There's better games for two players.

Best Use: A light, semi-conflict game when you need to loosed up a bit.

RATING: 6
A fairly light tactical game with a great theme and two parts: Part One has players placing their villages around Pompeii.  When Vesuvius erupts Part Two begins and players are trying to move their villagers out of Pompeii before the lava flow consumes them in flame.  The basic mechanic is safety in numbers: when placing one gets to place extra villagers if placed where others exist.  When moving players can move as far as the number of villagers on the space moved from.  UPDATE: bumped rating down a half point as there's just not enough real strategy and too much luck.  Rating would be much lower if it wasn't so quick with a great theme.

RATING: 8
[size=10][u][i][b]r{Initial Thoughts}r (after 5 plays):[/u][/b][/i][/size]
* Theme nicely integrated: you place people in Pompeii, then rush to evacuate them
* Tense and chaotic, with ample player screwage (ie tossing opponents into Vesuvius)
* Nice mechanic shift from one game phase to the next (area control then tile-laying)
* Setup is a bit of a pain (but necessary to denote different game phases)
* Good for lighter gamers and press-your-luck fans
* Initial rating: [b]7/10[/b]

[size=10][u][i][b]b{Further Thoughts}b (after 25 plays):[/u][/b][/i][/size]
* Still holds good replay value, and plays quickly with those familiar with the rules
* Shift in mechanics (card play to tile placement) makes for a unique gameplay 
* Even after 25+ plays, doesn't show any signs of being ignored/traded
* Good experiences with both light gamers (parents) and heavy gamers alike
* Further rating: [b]8/10[/b]

RATING: 7.5
DoP is a good game for families. That's the very first thing I have to say as the game has just enough fun with the volcano mechanism a chief part of the game play. There is nothing like burning your opponents meeples to death to bring about some family fun and get the comments flowing around the table. :)

The biggest asset of this game is that once everyone knows the rules to the game it moves along as a very quick pace. Yes, there is some downtime as you wait for your turn to come around to make you moves but the decisions in this game aren't rocket science... place a meeple, pick a card... place a lava tile... move your meeples to safety... burn an opponent's family members once in a while... repeat often. The actions don't take that long to decide and it's fun to watch the board take shape and see meeples getting charcoaled in Vesuvius along the way.  

The game isn't overly complicated but like any good game... there is enough strategy to make you think about what areas to occupy and there is real tension in the "Run for your lives" stage where you are hoping your little pieces aren't burnt to a crisp by your evil opponents.

Overall a great little family game and a pretty solid gateway style game for non-gamers as well. There is just enough confrontation and the potential for some evil yet strategic moves combined with a decent theme that this game should be a pretty easy sell to a fairly broad range of gamers.

RATING: 8
A clever game depicting the destruction of Pompeii.  The two phases of the game population and then destruction, are really well balanced.  Don't think that the population phase is just get as many pieces down.  You need to limit your opponents while trying to get the best positions.  The destruction phase is fun, placing lava tiles to pressure, block or destroy your opponents pieces is a whole lot of fun (especially if sound effects are thrown in).  

In our first game, I had the wonderful honour of toasting the first victims.  I placed the lava tile and grabbed those two suckers while making volcano and screaming sound effects.  There was deathly silence from my opponents.  I became concerned.  Was I too flippant about death? Was I showing no respect to those poor residents of Pompeji and the terrible pain they faced.  No. The silence was based on the fact that my opponents had no idea why I was toasting my own people.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Brilliant, brutal fun!
While essentially a simple and light filler, Der Untergang von Pompeji nevertheless requires some tactical thinking. Luck of the draw (in both cards and lava tiles) has a significant impact in the overall flow of the game, but a clever player can usually take advantage of any situation. Granted, our first game was, somewhat discouragingly, a complete and utter tie, but by the third game, my wife was able to sweep over a dozen of my people off the board with a single well-placed tile and secure a staggering win - mainly because I wasn't paying enough attention to the placement of my pieces.
Pompeji is a deceptively simple game with plenty of room for clever play. It might be just a bit too light and fast for me to ever be really good at, but I don't mind. I just like tossing people into a volcano.

RATING: 6.5
This is a light game based upon the small village of Pompeii that was wiped out during the eruption of Mt Vesuvius. Players first palce meeples into the buildings of Pompeii depending on the location cards they have. In the second phase of the game, players place lava tiles which may trap or engulf meeples. Player can move two of their own meeples per turn to get them out of the city and whoever has the most meeples out wins. 

There is a lot of luck in this game, but the geography of where the lava tiles start may favour one side where to initially place meeples. It's light, and can be fun in the right environment.

Quick, easy and very entertaining.  What this game lacks in depth it makes up for in speed of play. Okay, so the screams are simulated - but that just makes it all the better.

RATING: 7
The Downfall Of Pompeii is on par with its contemporary, Survive: Escape From Atlantis. Both have a similar concept and mechanics. Where Pompeii suffers by comparison is in the components; while not ugly by any means, they aren't as lovely as those in Survive. I do feel that Pompeii scores over Survive in that Pompeii is less likely to force the repeated victimization of a single opponent due to how the lava works compared to Survive's sea creatures.

One real downside I feel Pompeii has is that half the game is extended setup. That is not to say that it is boring, but you might have to field some questions of "So, when do we actually get to play this game?"
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I love that the back story for this game makes sense with the game play.  After the first volcano eruption people thought it was OK to start moving back into the city (1st part of the game).  This is when the players are trying to populate the city with as many pawns of their color as possible, after all the more you have in the city...the more you may be able to get OUT of the city.

The second part of the game is when the second volcanic eruption occurs and it is now time to evacuate the city again!  Everyone takes turns moving their pawns out of the city, whomever escapes with the most pawns intact, wins!

Very clever game with nice strategic elements, soaking in theme, and played in 30-45 minutes.

RATING: 8
The game goes in two phases. First you populate the city of Pompej and then volcano erupts and you (try to) evacuate your people. The game goes in about 30-45 minutes. There is plenty of randomness (the cards, drawing lava tiles) and you are more likely to win if you begin phase 2 and/or get to draw most Omen cards. But the game is short and fun enough game so this doesn't bother as much.

I particularly like how the theme is on the evil side and you can make nasty moves for opponents but overall feel of the game is still much more fun than cutthroath. The game has a nice story arch for such a simple, short and pretty abstract game.

The game works well with 3 or 4. A little bit less control with 4 players but it almost fits the theme and the game is fun to play either way.

RATING: 8
[b]The Downfall of Pompeii[/b] was traded away in a math trade 10/5/15. (Received Marvel VS 2PCG)
Received in a math trade (9/22/14).

[COLOR=#FF0000]A year later... thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]This game lasted a year in our collection and we really enjoyed our 10 plays (in fact this is a game my dad played with us). I have to admit that after the last few plays we decided that we played the game out. Yes there is randomness in each game based on the card draw and tile selection/placement, but the game started to feel samey. We all new where the best spots on the board were and even throwing other players people into the volcano started to lose it's charm. All that said I would still recommend this game to other families, just go into knowing that it will likely have a limited number of plays in it for you but I'm sure you'll enjoy the ride.

I also need to admit that I may have been hasty getting rid of Survive: Escape from Atlantis! which received twice as many plays as Pompeii before I traded it. Looking back Survive definitely had a lot more variety in the way the game played out. I would consider getting another copy since it was a game that we played a lot with our extended family (especially once we got the 5/6 player expansion.)[/i]

[COLOR=#FF0000]Initial thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]- Fun! Everyone loves throwing meeples into the volcanoes and blocking other peoples paths to safety with a well placed lava tile.
- Another great family game; easy to teach with nice components (especially the volcano).
- My dad has had fun playing this with my kids. He enjoys games like this and Survive: Escape from Atlantis!.
- I like how the people placement works when you are able to place out "family" members if there are already people in a building.
- Love the tile placement for the lava flow after the volcano erupts (the opposite of Survive where you are removing tiles).[/i]
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Really could use some of the hidden scoring that Survive! has; without it, it's a tad obvious who's going to win. (6.5/10)

RATING: 7
This has some nice things to recommend it, including the theme and the roasting of dudes in the volcano. It's a tale of halves - placing dudes out (where the luck of the cards plays a part), and from the mid-way point, running the dudes out of there. Players get a chance who to roast through the game, so most games will end up being fairly even with leader bashing taking place, with maybe the player who gets lucky in avoiding the early volcano tiles getting the key edge. But for a 20 minute filler type game, this is fine. The game plays quickly and generates good fun. It's even decent as a light 2 player, but the luck here might play more of a part as there's less people to hit on any leader which may emerge as a result of card luck.

RATING: 7.5
The Downfall of Pompeii is a light family game that can turn cutthroat in a hurry. The choices in the beginning are simple; you play a card that shows a type of building on which you can place one of your citizens. The real fun begins when the volcano erupts. Here you’ll draw a volcano tile out of the bag, and then move two of your pieces, hopefully hedging them closer to safety while attempting to block other players’ pieces from escaping a fiery death. Despite its dog-eat-dog nature, The Downfall of Pompeii remains accessible enough for casual players to jump into while offering an experience aimed to satisfy players of any skill level. After all, is there really anything more satisfying than throwing your opponents’ pieces into a volcano?
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

The setup with stacking the deck and the whole seeding phase are probably too much work for such a light game, though.

RATING: 8
Cool game with theme dripping like hot magma.  (Or lava, whatever floats your boat.) Lots of luck involved (with the Omens and the tile draws).  Have only played once, so I'll need to play some more to see if my initial excitement holds up.  Have (finally) played more.  I like it best with 4 so far.  Pretty speedy game that reminds me more and more of Survive!, with luck mostly in the setup (though immense majorities of people in the city is by no means a guarantee of victory).  The race to flee the city is a bit more strategic than the setup and shows the pitfalls of putting too many people in the city in tough spaces.

In a 4-player game, I only had 16 people out there and managed to get 10 out, while two others with 21 and 22 respectively, only managed to get 7 and 9 out.  (I lost by 1 to the other player, who got 11 of 19 out.)  Fewer people therefore does not necessarily mean defeat.  This (somewhat anecdotal) fact and the game's fun-ness has me boost it to an 8.

RATING: 7
Simple, but interesting and rather unique game, combining card playing and tile laying. It has basically two phases. On the first, you are populating Pompeii with your tokens (and sometimes removing your opponents' ones) through the use of cards. When the "eruption card", comes out the second phase begins. Now you getting lava tiles from a bag (representing the progressive destruction of the city), placing them on the board in way that hampers your opponents while trying to get your people out of the city. Highly recommended for new players. My 6-year old loves it!

RATING: 8
I own the German edition - don't be afraid to order it if you can't speak German. 95% language independant, after a round you get what's going on.

'Pompeji', as it has come to be known, is quickly becoming one of my most prized games, and these are the reasons why:  Pompeji is easy to learn but difficult to master; the game plays quick and repeat games are feasible; the scalable, overlying strategy is easily grasped by kids, non-gamers, and tacticians alike; the game has two very different rounds; the game is ripe with theme.  Really, this is a game that I will recommend to everyone, and I feel lucky to have my copy.  However, hardcore gamers beware.. if you're looking for something that you can take seriously, this isn't it.. but for a night of gaming, it's a great one to put on the agenda.

When do I play this?:
Whenever I can.  I don't know how people can't like this game... well ... maybe I can, but I wouldn't want to associate myself with them. :D

RATING: 4
Utterly random game. Sure, it's light, family-friendly, has a funny(?) theme, and the joy(?) of throwing people in a cardboard volcano, but the rules make very little sense, it's draw-and-place (which offers only a little more choice than roll-and-move), and the randomness is only offset by a huge screw-you factor, meaning that if the random draw doesn't screw you, the other players will. That's not how you balance a game. I find it pointless and frustrating, but I guess that if you really, really just want to throw people in a volcano, this is the game for you.

RATING: 6
Update: Surprisingly, plays on Yucata are enjoyable because the theme still shines through the mechanics and visuals. Still it is anticlimactic, now fired by Flashpoint, though maybe interested in Great Fire of London for a more historical feel.

Unfortunately, despite the strong theme, so far (3 games in) there is no smoke to mask who will win the game, which leaves the game anitclimatic. The first phase is interesting as you try and set yourself up to increase your population with the relatives rule, though the omen cards can unbalance placements. Just when you think you can get your folks in, the volcano blows aaah. Then we're into the 2nd phase which has mechanics conducive to downtime:- draw tile and move 2 guys. Unfortunately, I've seen situations where players have group their people which then gives godspeed to another player's occupying piece. Provokes sooty black humour as you toss victims into the mouth of the volcano(and we've never needed to look in for tie breaks), but ultimately doesn't light my fire.

RATING: 7
A simple quick game. Has 2 primary phases. 
Using a card draw place pieces on the board. Having precognition, your placement is with an eye for a quick exit.
The next phase - lava tiles come out destroying all in place. Your pieces need to head for the gates. The number of pieces in the location determine how far you can move, so it is best to leave your neighbors to their fiery fate.

Sound effects as citizens encounter the volcano, as are comments on hot tubs or hot footing it are a must.

RATING: 8
A game that is easy to under-rate, as the first English translation got the set-up rules completely wrong (turning people off the game when it first came out), and even with the right rules it seems devoid of any real decisions.

Not so - your placement in the first half of the game has a big impact on the second, and there's a lot of risk analysis and mitigation that can be done to make sure that you score as well as you can.

It's no heavyweight gamers' game, but it IS a good family-weight game - probably the best of 2004 (though I am also partial to 80 Days).  I find that I enjoy it far more than the author's Carcassonne! 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Un legame (cosa insolita) ben strutturato con l'ambientazione, che si sente molto, una piccola perla non molto conosciuta. Nel complesso il gioco è ben riuscito. La fortuna ha il suo peso, ma per vincere serve soprattutto una buona strategia. RATING: 6
It's often hard to convince my game group to play confrontational games, but everyone seemed to enjoy tossing eachother's pieces into the volcano. The game is light and fast enough to relieve a lot of the tension that usually comes with the types of games. The first phase of the game seems to drag a little bit, since piece placement isn't terribly important when the volcano tiles are random. The fun is definitely in the eruption/escape phase.

As enjoyable as this is, I think I prefer Survive: Escape from Atlantis over Pompeii when it comes to out-fleeing natural disasters in my board games.

RATING: 7
An interesting, two-stage game. In stage one, you place your Romans around the city of Pompeii using a deck of cards. In the deck of cards are two "AD 79" cards. Once the second one hits the table, the volcano explodes and stage two begins. In stage two you move your Romans out of the city, and draw lava tiles to place on the board killing Romans and blocking them off from exiting the city. 

It is a fun game that plays best with 4 players.

RATING: 5
Seems like a light, fun game with the fantastic theme of throwing people into lava to win the game. It's totally worth having for that reason alone. And it might actually be a good game to introduce a newer player to the boardgaming hobby.

After a second play, it seems that throwing people in lava doesn't rescue a relatively weak game. There is better fare for new entrants to the hobby. In particular, setting the deck between plays and explaining three different sets of rules for three different mini-games (phases of the game) speaks against its usability as a gateway game.

For a regular game, it's too light, and although you can come up with a few "neat" ways to help your people escape, it's not very challenging.

RATING: 7
Seemingly too-long rules for a pretty simple fun eurogame that was enjoyable to play.  (And calling your extra people "relatives" was just plain confusing.)

In the first half, players put their dudes into buildings.  In the second half, lava starts flowing and dudes flee to escape the city.  The lava flow is a clever combination of randomness and player controlled mayhem to cover or surround other players' dudes.  Good fun (even if the theme is rather morbid if you think about it), especially when you get to throw someone's dude into the paper cone volcano.

RATING: 6
This is by Wrede, designer of Carcassonne. The game is divided into two parts. We didn't know how the second part worked until we started it, so we had no idea what or why we were doing in the first part, sort of like the first time playing Dvonn. In the first part you put your people in the town. In the second you move them out as the lava flows.

While similar in theme and some ideas to the other Pompeii game I played (Last 37 Minutes, which I didn't like), this one offers you more control. I suspect that now that I know what I'm doing, the game will make some sense the next few times I try it. On the other hand, it also looks like the game is rather limited in depth and won't withstand more than ten or so plays, altogether. I will have to play it more times to confirm this.
