RATING: 6
The Downfall of Pompeii is an entertaining social entry into the gaming field. It's very light, and chance plays a tremendous role despite the appearance of self-determination. Around a table of roughly equal players, the winner will be determined largely by chance and by who chooses to victimize whom when the Omen cards are drawn. If you try to play this game competitively and strategically, you are in for a major let down. So don't. Instead, just kick back, throw screaming meeples hex-cylinders into the volcano, and have some fun. It's a relaxing social game which doesn't make you think too hard, and plays very quick. In other words, Downfall is a great filler. Personally, I don't want to play fillers that often, so no matter how excellently they are designed I can't get all that jazzed about playing them. I just really groove on mental stimulation - but this game is a perfect breath of fresh air if you need a break from intensity. It is also an excellent game to play with kids, as your masterplans can be easily foiled, thus allowing a little bit of youth victory to occur now and then. So it's much better as a family game than many Euros.

Sok jót hallottam már róla, de nem gondoltam, hogy ennyire jó kis játék lesz ez a 2004-ben kiadott társas. Embereinket telepítjük Pompejibe, ami mellett nemsokára kitör a vulkán és menekülnünk kell. Érdekes téma nagyon jó megvalósítással. Több fázisban kerülnek fel az embereink Pompeji házaiba, majd a vulkánkitörés után menekülünk és tereljük a lávát az ellenfelek emberei felé a mieinktől minél távolabb. Meglepő módon a két eddig játszott parti nagyon kiegyenlített lett, pedig a szerencse szerepét nem kicsinek érzem több helyen sem a játékban. Nagyon konfliktusos játék, azonban ha a játékosok nem személy okokból vezérelve indulnak el egymás ellen, akkor tényleg nagyon izgalmas játék sülhet ki a Pompeji bukásából. Nagyon tematikus, jól adja vissza a szörnyű esemény izgalmát a játék. Nagyon gyors, második játékra már simán lemehet 1 óra alatt és nagyon változatos minden parti. Mindenképp ajánlott a játék azoknak, akik nem félnek némi konfliktustól.

RATING: 8
I have to love any game where you get to scream "Your ass got Magma'ed!"  If you like moving pieces around on a board running from hot lava, this game is for you.  Many fun choices trying to work against the player controlled AI of the the lava flow.  

People complain about the set up phase, but I see no problems in it.  I think it rather fun and relaxing, getting you ready for the big blow.  A strong playing in the first phase will help you quite a bit in the second (which seems more than reasonable to me).  There is more to the first phase than just setting your guys up by the exits.  Regardless, it is a lot of random and a touch chaotic, but for me once you accept it there is a joy in running your pieces around the city.  

This is the kind of game that Milton Bradley needs to be making.  If you love Survive!, this should be as much of a pleasure.

Overall it is grand fun, but I do have to say that there is the potential of A/P.  Nothing too serious, but it is there.

RATING: 8.5
I finally own this game!  It's been on my radar for ages, at last I had the opportunity to play it, and I was still surprised by how much I enjoyed it!  It takes 2 distinct phases, combines a few very interesting mechanics, and adds just the right amount of luck and strategy to create a very fun and slightly brain-burning little game (perhaps caused by all the lava).  And speaking of lava, you get to throw your opponents' people into a volcano!  (Other Euro-styled games ought to take note of this!)  Besides the volcano, the game components are quite basic (although I've ordered 140 meeples to replace the people tokens), but you don't really notice the lack of production value because you are having so much fun!  I've used a lot of exclamation marks in this mini review!  That alone should indicate my enthusiasm with this game!  Game design: 4.5/5  Personal enjoyment: 4/5  Total: 8.5/10
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Amusing multi-stage family game where pawns are placed in buildings in Pompeii and then must escape it in the face of oncoming lava. The final stage, where pawns can move as many spaces as the number of pawns in their starting space, is a particularly engaging exercise in shared incentives. Staying close to other players discourages them from placing lava nearby, but may enable them to run further (leaving you behind!) or simply present a richer target for other opponents. Throwing poor dead citizens into the volcano is a particularly nice touch. 

Ultimately there is far too much luck for my taste but I would be most intrigued in a variant with neither cards nor random tiles.

RATING: 5
A fun game reminiscent of the Parker Brothers classic, Survive! You spend the first half of the game placing your people in an area where you KNOW a volcanic eruption is imminent. How nice. The second half of the game is pure Survive! Get yer critters out of dodge while throwing your opponents' critters under the bus, er, lava.
Like I said, fun game, but I would have liked if the first half was a little more elegant. The setup is a bit tedious and the rules for placing "relatives" could have been a lot cleaner. I'm also slightly (ever so slightly) worried that it could have severe kingmaking issues. To be fair, Survive! also has these issues, but to a much lower degree because the values of the critters are unknown. Pompeii has much more open information. If Wolfgang Kramer had designed this, it could have been an all-time classic. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 10
New. (trade for MTG)

Can you make a game that involves a group of people that all die in a natural disaster and enjoy dropping opponents in a volcano? The Downfall of Pompeii!!!

Game is played in two-stages.

Stage 1: Players load up Pompeii with as many of their clan as possible and as close to exits as possible. I guess those people knew that they might need an escape from Pompeii. Draw an omen and you get to pick a Joe to put......IN-THE-VOLCANO!!!! Loading your "family" is a little wonky.

Stage B: This is the fun part. The volcano erupts any you take turns putting lava on your opponents and select the two people in your family worth saving...this turn. If your block-eeple is around more block-eeples they can move faster. Again a little Timey-Whimey. 

Even thought theme has a few weird plot issues, it is a blast to play.

See what I did there?

RATING: 7
This is compared to Survive a lot, but I think Pompeii is a better version of this mechanic--maybe just because you get to throw people in a volcano, which is somewhat more satisfying than merely feeding them to sea monsters. Pompeii is played in two stages and therefore feels almost like two different games. The first part is intricate and a little dull compared to the last part; it's all about placement. When the volcano blows, it's a free-for-all to get out of the city while destroying your opponents when the lava flow. So it's flawed, but a lot of fun.

RATING: 7
Quick and easy game, quite luck based. Setup (shuffling) more complicated than necessary, but still OK. 
First half of game: Place people on board (wooden cylinders), cards determine where you may place them. If you get a good placement, you get additional people in. Second half of game: Draw lava tiles and place them, then move your people out of the city. Movement points depend on number of people on the same area. This part is mostly push-your-luck: Which people to rescue immediately, which to give up. Recommended as gateway, but also enjoyed by frequent players.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
This is a pretty light game that most non-gamers will enjoy and agree to play again. There is very minimal stradegy involved in the game. The game is played quick and taught in just a few minutes. The game plays in two phases. First phase placing all your people on the map. Second phase getting your people to escape when the volcano errupts. The erruption happens randomly, and several times when I have played the volcano errupts before you can get a decent amount of people on the board. When the volcano errupts to soon it can really ruin the game. You might want to modify the rules a bit in order to make the volcano errupt later in the game.

RATING: 8

A fun game.

Update: More plays, more fun. The rating has moved from a 7.5 to an 8. One of the problems with having a large game collection is that some games just don't get as much play as they should.



Suitability for Travel:

I have a 1 to 5 scale for four categories (1 is worst, 5 is best) in order of importance:

Portability (the less luggage space the better) - 1
Footprint (the less table space when playing the better) - 2
Scalability (the wider range of player counts the better) - 3
Learnability (the easier to teach non-gamers the better) - 3


Overall - 1

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
[thing=13004][/thing] is a simple, interactive and fun game: the goal is to save as many people from the fury of the volcano as possible. 

There are three phases in the game: in the first, only one people at a time is placed, accordingly with a card used (each player has a number of them in hand, and each has a number correlated with places on the board). In the second phase, people are added faster, as extra markers are put for each other people already in the same place a player adds her own. Finally, in the third phase, the volcano detonates and starts to kill people - no more markers are put, and players, now, try move the ones they have out of the city, as volcano tiles are constantly placed, killing and/or blocking the people and putting pressure in the players. Killed people goes into the volcano, and serve as a tie breaker at the end of the game. The person that saves the most people, will be the winner.

[thing=13004][/thing] has two parts with loads of luck built in - the draw of cards and of volcano tiles. Still, is normally more important to recognize and seize opportunities and they appear, both for the placement of people and with the timming of moving them - as the rule of movement is pretty clever and gives importance to planning wisely the placement of people: when a marker is moved, it can move a number of squares equal to the total number of markers in the spot it started. Simple and efficient in creating tension, interaction and in requering a sharp eye to seek the best opportunities, be for gain more movement, be to reduce the movement of others.

There are, however, two problems with [thing=13004][/thing]: the first I already mentioned, which is the luck factor. It is present in the draw of cards, that can put a serious limitation in what places you can add people, both in phases one and two; and there are also the Omen cards, that let you kill one people of other player - just like that. Also, the draw of volcano tiles can harm or help a lot one or more players. Nonetheless, [thing=13004][/thing] doens't present itself as heavily strategic, nor with great control or perfect information. It is a light game, with direct attacks, and fun due to all the destruction, running and tossing with satisfaction markers inside the volcano. Thus the random elements serve to increase the replay value, as new paths to place and flee must be taken in each play.

In the end, [thing=13004][/thing] pleased me a great deal, with its uncompromised nature, giving entertainment coupled with tatical decisions in search of windows of opportunity to overcame the others. It isn't perfect, nor will work for everyone, due to luck elements and agressive interaction. For me it worked in allowing some easy, quick paced and effective fun. Recommended.

RATING: 8
This game is a unique, 2-phase game about Vesuvius wiping out the city of Pompeii. There is a very even blend of luck and strategy. This game has the ability to bring good post-game disussions. With the right group, it can be a game of giddy enjoyment as you anticipate various points of calamity throughout the game. This is a wonderful design by Klaus-Jurgen Wrede.

Since introducing this to my gaming group, two other people have bought it. This game has one of the best integration of themes and mechanics I've ever seen. Almost as theme-rich as Plunder, but much simpler in terms of rules. Such a great design.

RATING: 7
Don't let looks deceive you - this game is quite a bit more thrilling and devious than you would expect judging it by its looks (the slightly boring looking cards and board)! Perfectly playable with two, in which case your first game should take around 60 minutes. The game is easy to explain and moves along at a brisk pace. Will you save the lone villager who has almost been surrounded by lava, or will you move the community to safety first? Good stuff!
UPDATE: Only played with two players sofar. I expect that the game will be better with three, possibly worse with four (too much chaos). Each of our games invoked a pleasant feeling of urgency, but because of the randomness involved in citizen and lava placement, every now and than we play a pretty unbalanced game. Still one of my favorite two player games however.

RATING: 7
First play - 2 players - This has been getting alot of good buzz with my group so when Osiris Ra suggested we play a quick 2-player game of it I was in. The theme is great. Pompeii is about to be covered in lava. Place your men and then when the s*** hits the fan run them the hell out of there. It reminded me of Survive! The card playing aspect of it was a little dry. You play your cards and hope to gain extra men by placing one in a building that already has another man in it. Placing your man in a building that already has 3 gives you 3 extra men to place! Then when the volcano erupts the game gets really exciting. YOu have to run before the lava overtakes you and the lava is tiles drawn from the bag. Again luck is a big factor. Its a lot of fun (I did win) and I look forward to trying it with 3 or 4 players.

RATING: 5
The game has a lot of luck, but it plays quickly, and it's the sort of game where you hose each other anyway, so what difference does a little bit of bad luck make?  Plus, the fewer players you have in the game, the less chaos there's going to be.  It's reminiscent of Survive!, but it seems bit clunky right out of the box to understand.  It definitely takes a play to understand the flow of the game; by the second playing, we mostly had the flow of the game understood.  My biggest issue with the game is the convoluted way that you set up the deck of cards....

I should add that the first playing of this game left me wondering what I was missing, but by the second game, it made sense, and was a lot of fun.  If your first play was underwhelming, give it another try.

1 play: 3 players
2 plays: 4 players

RATING: 6
The Downfall of Pompeii has a lot in common with Survive!, if you've ever played that classic game. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is the lightest game I rate this high; it's just that darned fun.

I have only three complaints, all of which are relatively minor (and certainly don't affect play once the game's started).

1. The draw deck is just a tad complicated to set up, and requires several shuffles.

2. The game only goes to four players.

3. There aren't the same number of pieces of each color.  You can only play specific colors at each player count.  Only red and black have enough pieces for a two player game, for instance.  Since I only ever expect to play with the full four players, I don't think this will be an issue - it just bugs me.

Avoid bad losers when you play this game!

RATING: 7
Played several times (with 3 or 4 players). An enjoyable, if not very deep, game. I rather like how the way the board is divided changes as the game progresses. The end game, however, is both too random (the order in which the lava tiles are drawn  can have a huge influence on the final result) and too predictible (since the numbers of tiles of each sort are known exactly).

RATING: 6.5
Not something to play every day, but fun once in a while, mostly because of the excellent theme. To get the most enjoyment out of this game, you [i]must[/i] make sound effects each time a meeple dies or runs.

Plays well with kids. My daughter, who is almost 5 years old, likes it and can play by the full rules (with a tiny bit of help sometimes). If I played my hardest I could win easily, but if I just role play the little terrified meeples and making the moves that seem "most fun" instead of "most likely to win," then we have a fun, close game.

RATING: 5
Easy to learn with very simple mechanics.  I think the strategy to the game lay in the first phase, the placement of your people.  Since the amount of movement they can make during the second half is dependent on how many other pieces are in the same square, it is important that they don't get stranded.  The other thing to note is that having more pieces on the board isn't necessarily a good thing, due to the fact that the number of turns are limited by the tiles available.  I didn't really have fun with Pompeii, not something I would see myself playing any time soon again.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.1
在刚开始玩的时候，感觉这个游戏是不是有点太简单，weight太轻了，以至于对他300多名的高排名产生了一些质疑，但是随着游戏的推进，发现游戏是有几个策略点的。

第一个是利用亲友规则，尽可能的多塞人。

第二个则是逃跑时候精算移动力。这一点在玩的时候有种变体跳棋的感觉，这种搭桥蹭移动力的快感和德式打combo刷刷有异曲同工之妙，这点设计的很赞。

第三个是初始的布局，虽然靠近城门的位置看起来比较赞，但是也离火山喷发孔会比较近，因此可能来不及动就挂在滚滚的岩浆中。城中的建筑物比较远，但是容纳人的上限多，一旦人数起来了，你的移动力会变得很强，当然无论这个建筑容纳人数多或少，最后动的人肯定是很亏的。布局还是需要多多揣摩，并且要根据其他玩家的布局来调整自己的策略。

第四个是放置岩浆板块，有时候可以围杀一片别人的居民。

总体来说，这款游戏咋一看可能没有想象中那么对得起300名的排名。但是实际玩起来还是有很多优点和策略点的，长安灯上面已经点出。但是游戏还是偏向于一个抽象棋游戏的感觉，变化少了一些，没有多路线的广度思维，耐玩性略差了一些。
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
